/ 13	. 

/ Met injection	,

/ when you run an Angular appl, it creates a dependency injector. An injector is in charge of knowing how to create an send things.

car-parts.component.ts 			dep. injector 			racing-data.service.ts
   --------------------------->
	can I have a racing data service?
														Yes, I know how to get one	, he creates one and sends it over	,

	<-------------------------------------------------------
								a racing data service

car-cart.component.ts
   --------------------------->
	can I have a racing data service?
														Yes, I know how to get one	, it is already there	, and sends it over	, 

	<-------------------------------------------------------
								the same racing data service


/ How does a dep inj know what is can inject?
/ we have to tell it by registring providers with it	,

/ so	, 
dep inj	
	racing-data.service.ts
	another.service.ts
	api.service.ts

/ Dus we moeten van racing-data.service.ts een provider maken	,
/ We moeten	,
/ 1. 	Add the Injectable decorator to RacingDataService
/ 2	. Let the inj know about our service by naming it as a provider	,
/ 3	. Inject the dependency to our car-part.component.ts	,

/ ad 1	. 

$ vi app/racing-data.service.ts

import {CARPARTS}from './mocks';
import{Injectable}from'@angular/core';		<-
@Injectable()															<-
export class RacingDataService{
  getCarParts(){
    return CARPARTS;
}


/ ad 2	. we want all our components to have access to the service. So we register the service at the top level component as a provider	,

$ vi app/app.component.ts

import { Component } from '@angular/core';
import {CarPartsComponent} from './car-parts.component';
import {RacingDataService}from './racing-data.service';

@Component({
  selector:'my-app',
  template:` <h1>{{title}}</h1>
    <car-parts></car-parts> `,
  directives:[ CarPartsComponent ],
  providers:[RacingDataService]
})
export class AppComponent{
  title='Ultra Racing';
};

/ ad 3	.

[eric@almond app]$ vi racing-data.service.ts

import {CARPARTS}from './mocks';
import{Injectable}from'@angular/core';
import {Http} from '@angular/http';
import 'rxjs/add/operator/map';
@Injectable()
export class RacingDataService{
  constructor(private http:Http){			// (*)
	} 																	
  getCarParts(){
    //return CARPARTS;
    return this.http.get('app/car-parts.json')          // Observable, is like an Array ,
      .map(response=>
        <CarPart[]>response.json()      // for each response, parse the string into JSON  ,
        .data); 									// the array we want is under the data keyword	,
	}
}

/ (*) Omdat de service @Injectable	, kunnen we een dep geven , http hier	, 
/ TODO (Eerder 	, en deze is NIET @Injectable
export class CarPartsComponent{
  constructor(private racingDataService:RacingDataService){	


/ since our service now returns an observable object, we need to subscribe to that data stream and tell our component what to do when our data arrives	,

[eric@almond app]$ vi car-parts.component.ts
  ngOnInit(){
      this.racingDataService.getCarParts()
        .subscribe(carParts=>this.carParts=carParts);
  };
/ When carParts arrive on our data stream	, set it equal to our local carParts array (=this.carParts)	,

/ we zien	,

/ OK	, 

/ 1	. Error handling must still be done	,  
/ 2	. Since we isolated network calls as a service	,   we can substitude RacingDataService for RacingDataMockService	, if we want to test or work offline	,
/ 3	. learn Observables, when making a lot of http calls	, 

/ Finally:
/ 7	. Angular apps usually load data using service classes after the Angular app is initialized and running	, 
/ 7	. we can use the http library through dependency injection	, 
/ 7	. our http calls return an Observable, not a Promise	, which behaves more like an array	,

[eric@almond Flanagan]$ cat p168_2.js 

function R(w,h){
	this.w=w;
	this.h=h;
}
R.prototype.a=function(){
	return this.w*this.h;
}

function PR(x,y,w,h){
	R.call(this,w,h);
	this.x=x;
	this.y=y;
}

var f=function(){}
f.prototype=R.prototype;	
PR.prototype=new f();

PR.prototype.constructor=PR	// was f

PR.prototype.contains=function(x,y){
	this.x<=x && x<=this.x+this.width && this.y<=y && y<=this.y+this.height;
}

var pr=new PR(1,2,11,12);
var a=pr.area();
var b=pr.constains(5,7);

function PR(x,y,w,h){
  PR.superclass=R;
  arguments.callee.superclass.call(this,w,h);
  this.x=x;
  this.y=y;
}

/ Inderdaad	, node_modules is rm uit github repo	,


/ 13	. 
/ Lees	,
http://stackoverflow.com/questions/6313126/how-to-remove-a-directory-in-my-github-repository

/ we hadden moeten doen	, (dan blijft in local file system)	,
git rm -r --cached myFolder
git commit -m "Removed folder from repository"
git push origin master

To ignore that folder from next commits make one file in root named .gitignore and put that folders name into it. You can put as many as you want
.gitignore file will be look like this

/FolderName

/ 13	 .

/ Lees	,

https://git-scm.com/docs/gitignore

A gitignore file specifies intentionally untracked files that Git should ignore. Files already tracked by Git are not affected; see the NOTES below for details.

/ 13	. 

/ 'n array's length is alleen set als de key is (convertable) to a integer	, dus '0' is ook OK	,
/ een array kan een property hebben	, maar is geen 'onderdeel' van het array	,

/ 

_b['name']=7
VM30631:1 Uncaught ReferenceError: _b is not defined(…)

/ een array is een special obj	, met numerical keys	,  die je als enigste ziet als je het array print, of die contribute to .length	, 
/ je kunt een array ook een property geven	, name bijv	, 

/ Of je nou een Array maakt of algemener een Object	, dan moet je deze eerst def	,
_b['name']=7
VM30631:1 Uncaught ReferenceError: _b is not defined(…)
/ we moeten dus eerst	, 
_b=[]
/ of	, 
_b['foo','bar']
/ of 
_x={}
/ of	, 
_x={name:'foo'}

/ We kunnen in de DOM eigen custom tags add	, like <foo/>


$('body').append('<div>Foo Bar</div>')
/ OK
$('body').append('<foo>Bar</foo>')
/ OK
$('foo').css('color','red')
/ OK	, 
/ we zien Bar in de browser in het rood	, 



/ we zien in HTML	,
<body>
	...
	<div>Foo Bar</div>
	<foo>Bar</foo>
</body>
